[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#Here's the candidate coaching session, it's probably the best place to start: http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oWbUtlUhwa8&feature=youtu.be|Here's the candidate coaching session, it's probably the best place to start: http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oWbUtlUhwa8&feature=youtu.be]]
[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#Our interview style may differ from what you've experienced elsewhere, and tends to be highly technical. The interviewer will be interested in the specifics of your past projects, implementations and how you arrived at your conclusions. Your phone interview will cover data structures and algorithms (i.e. Big-O Notation). You may be asked to write code. The phone screen may include topics such as coding, data structures, algorithms, computer science theory, and systems design. It is also recommended that you review Big-O notations also known as "the run time characteristic of an algorithm." Also, one of our senior engineers has recommended candidates read "Programming Interviews Exposed: Secrets to Landing Your Next Job" by John Mongan and Noah Suojanen to give you an edge--it's likely a good book to have in general.  Two other books that may be helpful are: "Programming Pearls" by Jon Bentley -Programming questions that get you thinking outside of the box; and lastly, "Cormen/Leiserson/Rivest/Stein: Introduction to Algorithms" or the CLR textbook|Our interview style may differ from what you've experienced elsewhere, and tends to be highly technical. The interviewer will be interested in the specifics of your past projects, implementations and how you arrived at your conclusions. Your phone interview will cover data structures and algorithms (i.e. Big-O Notation). You may be asked to write code. The phone screen may include topics such as coding, data structures, algorithms, computer science theory, and systems design. It is also recommended that you review Big-O notations also known as "the run time characteristic of an algorithm." Also, one of our senior engineers has recommended candidates read "Programming Interviews Exposed: Secrets to Landing Your Next Job" by John Mongan and Noah Suojanen to give you an edge--it's likely a good book to have in general.  Two other books that may be helpful are: "Programming Pearls" by Jon Bentley -Programming questions that get you thinking outside of the box; and lastly, "Cormen/Leiserson/Rivest/Stein: Introduction to Algorithms" or the CLR textbook]]
[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#Our interviews tend to involving coding into either a Google doc or a whiteboard--from what other Engineers have told me this is a skill that is invaluable to practice and get comfortable with ahead of the interviews|Our interviews tend to involving coding into either a Google doc or a whiteboard--from what other Engineers have told me this is a skill that is invaluable to practice and get comfortable with ahead of the interviews]]
[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#Here's a pretty good list of some old (and no longer used) interview questions that should provide nice practice coding: http://www.careercup.com|Here's a pretty good list of some old (and no longer used) interview questions that should provide nice practice coding: http://www.careercup.com]]
[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#I have heard that this book can be very helpful|I have heard that this book can be very helpful]]
[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#Also make sure to check out our Google C++/Python code style guides|Also make sure to check out our Google C++/Python code style guides]]
[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#For Java we don't publish anything official, however we base it heavily on|For Java we don't publish anything official, however we base it heavily on]]
[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#It may also be worth refreshing on hash tables, heaps, binary trees, linked lists, depth-first search, recursion (basically CS 101...concepts that everyone knows but sometimes doesn't come right off the tip of one's tongue at a moments notice). For more information on Algorithms you can visit: http://www.topcoder.com/tc?module=Static&d1=tutorials&d2=alg_index|It may also be worth refreshing on hash tables, heaps, binary trees, linked lists, depth-first search, recursion (basically CS 101...concepts that everyone knows but sometimes doesn't come right off the tip of one's tongue at a moments notice). For more information on Algorithms you can visit: http://www.topcoder.com/tc?module=Static&d1=tutorials&d2=alg_index]]
[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#Here's a video algorithms course from MIT: http://tinyurl.com/2cg4yo9|Here's a video algorithms course from MIT: http://tinyurl.com/2cg4yo9]]
[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#Many of the questions asked in Google interviews are open-ended because our engineers are looking to see how you engage the problem. Be sure to talk through your thought process about the questions you are asked, as well as your approach to problems and solutions. Ask specific questions if you need more clarification|Many of the questions asked in Google interviews are open-ended because our engineers are looking to see how you engage the problem. Be sure to talk through your thought process about the questions you are asked, as well as your approach to problems and solutions. Ask specific questions if you need more clarification]]
[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep|2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep]]		[[2015.05 GoogleInterviewPrep#Think about ways to improve the solution you'll present. In many cases, the first answer that springs to mind may need some refining. It is worthwhile to talk about your initial thoughts to a question. A brute force explanation will be received less well than taking time to compose a more efficient solution. Ask clarifying questions if you do not understand the problem or need more information. Many of the questions asked in Google interviews are deliberately underspecified because our engineers are looking to see how you engage the problem. In particular, they are looking to see which areas leap to your mind as the most important piece of the technological puzzle you've been presented|Think about ways to improve the solution you'll present. In many cases, the first answer that springs to mind may need some refining. It is worthwhile to talk about your initial thoughts to a question. A brute force explanation will be received less well than taking time to compose a more efficient solution. Ask clarifying questions if you do not understand the problem or need more information. Many of the questions asked in Google interviews are deliberately underspecified because our engineers are looking to see how you engage the problem. In particular, they are looking to see which areas leap to your mind as the most important piece of the technological puzzle you've been presented]]
